The following pages represent the text of a work on Dharmas─Бstra by the great Nanda alias Vin─Бyaka Pandit of the Dharm─Бdhik─Бr─л family of Benares. The work deals with certain details1 & others.")connected with the observance of the Navaratra rites. These details have been well brought out in the Sanskrit Introduction prefixed to the work & need not be repeated here.

The author lived in Benares in the 17th Century of the Christian era & was universally respected as the leading pandit of the age in Northern India, specially on questions connected with Hindu Law. He was the author of several works, mostly on Dharma SтАЩ─Бstra, the only exception being his M─Бdhav─Бnanda Mah─Бk─Бvya. His ancestor Pandit Lakс╣гm─лdhara, a M─Бh─Бr─Бс╣гtra Br─Бhmana of the Mudgala family, was one of the most celebrated scholars of Bidar in Southern India & was recipient of high honours from the Emperor of Delhi. He was recognised in those days as the highest & final authority on Hindu Law. His younger son Govinda migrated to Benares, on the death of his elder son SтАЩr─л Kс╣Ыс╣гс╣Зa, together with the latterтАЩs inтАУ

тАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФ

*These details bear upon the determination of the tithis. So far as the Pratipat is concerned the author is in favour, when it is not available in its purity, of it being connected with Am─Б rather than with Dvit─лy─Б*. The Navar─Бtra Vrata is held by him to be a species of тАЬNakta Vrata.тАЭ Regarding the P─Бraс╣З─Б day the author prefers the Navam─лagainst the DasтАЩam─лas in the opinion of Kamal─Бkara Bhatta, Raghunandana & others.The Navami view is supported by Ananta Deva (Smс╣Ыtikaustabha) & others.*

fant son Mah─лpati. The author of the present work is the great grand-son of this Mah─лpati.

The family of Nanda Pandit had been a votary of Sri R─Бma. But since he obtained three images of Mah─Б Viс╣гс╣Зu at Pray─Бga (Triveс╣З─л) the family has been a worshipper of SтАЩr─л Kс╣Ыс╣гс╣Зa. The Janm─Бс╣гс╣нami ceremony of SтАЩr─л Kс╣Ыс╣гс╣Зa, which was commenced by Nanda Pandit, is still continued in the family.

The author flourished at a time when Benares was the home of Sanskrit Learning. During his life time (1550тАУ1630A.D.) Benares was the seat of literary activities of some of the greatest figures in the history of Sanskrit Literature. N─Бr─Бyaс╣Зa Bhaс╣нс╣нa & his son Sankara Bhatta I, Vidy─Бniv─Бsa BhattacharyaтАФ the father of Vi┼Ыvanatha Nyayasiddhantapa├▒chanana, Nrsimh─Бsrama,the author of Bhedadhikk─Бra, Advaitaс╕Н─лpik─Б and Vedantatattvaviveka, Madhusudana Sarasvati, Nilakaс╣Зс╣нha Daivaj├▒a,the author of Nilakaс╣Зс╣нhi T─Бjika,Muh┼лrtachintamani & the court astronomer of the Emperor Akbar, were some of the most illustrious contemporaries of Nanda Pandit.

Nanda Pandit lived in the end of the 16th and in the beginning of the 17th century, the date of his commentary on Visnu Smrti being 1622 A.D.A manuscript of the Dharm─Бdhik─Бr─л Vam┼Ыacharita, written by one Venir─Бma Pandit, is available. It is a descriptive account of the family beginning with Pandit Lakс╣гmidhara of Bidar, the 5th ancestor of Nanda Pandit Dharm─Бdhik─Бri.From this it appears that the family has been famous from the days of Lakс╣гmidhara for proficiency in Dharma┼Ы─БтАУ

stra learning and that it has been a Vaiс╣гс╣Зava family with R─Бmachandra as its family deity. A list of Nanda PanditтАЩs works has been supplied in the Sanskrit Introduction, to which may be added the name of M─Бmsam─лm─Бс╣Зs─Б,a work2 mentioned in his own SтАЩr─Бddhakalpalat─Б.
